0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;border-top:#aaa 1px solid; border-bottom:#aaa 1px solid;">\n<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Decline Thesis">Historiography</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Template:History of the Ottoman Empire"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Template talk:History of the Ottoman Empire"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The&#160;<b>Ottoman Empire</b>&#160;(<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\x92/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">\xc9\x92</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span lang="ota" dir="rtl">\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xab\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xdb\x8c\xd9\x87</span>&#8206;, <i><i lang="ota-Latn" title="Ottoman Turkish-language transliteration">Devlet-i \xca\xbfAl\xc4\xabye-i \xca\xbfOsm\xc4\x81n\xc4\xabye</i></i>, literally <b>The Exalted Ottoman State</b>; <a href="/wiki/Modern_Turkish" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Turkish">Modern Turkish</a>: <i><i lang="tr" title="Turkish language text">Osmanl\xc4\xb1 \xc4\xb0mparatorlu\xc4\x9fu</i></i> or <i><i lang="tr" title="Turkish language text">Osmanl\xc4\xb1 Devleti</i></i>), also historically known in Western Europe as the <b>Turkish Empire</b><sup id="cite_ref-Hamish_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamish-13">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> or simply <b>Turkey</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> was a state that controlled much of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> between the 14th and early 20th centuries. It was founded at the end of the 13th century in northwestern <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in the town of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6%C4%9F%C3%BCt" title="S\xc3\xb6\xc4\x9f\xc3\xbct">S\xc3\xb6\xc4\x9f\xc3\xbct</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Bilecik_Province" title="Bilecik Province">Bilecik Province</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Oghuz_Turks" title="Oghuz Turks">Oghuz Turkish</a> tribal leader <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> After 1354, the Ottomans crossed into <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and with the conquest of <a href="/wiki/The_Balkans" class="mw-redirect" title="The Balkans">the Balkans</a>, the Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_beyliks" title="Anatolian beyliks">beylik</a> was transformed into a transcontinental empire. The Ottomans ended the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> with the 1453 <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">conquest of Constantinople</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Quataert2005_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quataert2005-16">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 16th and 17th centuries, at the height of its power under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> the Ottoman Empire was a multinational, multilingual empire controlling most of Southeast Europe, parts of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, Western Asia, parts of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, North Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of the 17th century, the empire contained <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Provinces of the Ottoman Empire">32 provinces</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Vassal_and_tributary_states_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Vassal and tributary states of the Ottoman Empire">vassal states</a>. Some of these were later absorbed into the Ottoman Empire, while others were granted various types of autonomy during the course of centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;note 6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With <a href="/wiki/Constantinople_during_the_Ottoman_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantinople during the Ottoman era">Constantinople</a> as its capital and control of lands around the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean basin</a>, the Ottoman Empire was at the centre of interactions between the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> worlds for six centuries. While the empire was once thought to have entered a period of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Decline Thesis">decline</a> following the death of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>, this view is no longer supported by the majority of academic historians.<sup id="cite_ref-decline_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decline-20">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The empire continued to maintain a flexible and strong economy, society and military throughout the 17th and much of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However, during a long period of peace from 1740 to 1768, the Ottoman military system fell behind that of their European rivals, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian</a> empires.<sup id="cite_ref-AksanOW_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AksanOW-22">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Ottomans consequently suffered severe military defeats in the late 18th and early 19th centuries, which prompted them to initiate a comprehensive process of reform and modernisation known as the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a>. Thus, over the course of the 19th century, the Ottoman state became vastly more powerful and organised, despite suffering further territorial losses, especially in the Balkans, where a number of new states emerged.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The empire allied with <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> in the early 20th century, hoping to escape from the diplomatic isolation which had contributed to its recent territorial losses, and thus joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> on the side of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> While the Empire was able to largely hold its own during the conflict, it was struggling with internal dissent, especially with the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Revolt" title="Arab Revolt">Arab Revolt</a> in its Arabian holdings. During this time, atrocities were committed by the Ottoman government against the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_genocide" title="Assyrian genocide">Assyrians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Pontic Greeks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Empire\'s defeat and the occupation of part of its territory by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">aftermath of World War I</a> resulted in <a href="/wiki/Partitioning_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Partitioning of the Ottoman Empire">its partitioning</a> and the loss of its Middle Eastern territories, which were <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="Sykes\xe2\x80\x93Picot Agreement">divided between the United Kingdom and France</a>. The successful <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> against the occupying Allies led to the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a> in the Anatolian heartland and the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_sultanate" title="Abolition of the Ottoman sultanate">abolition of the Ottoman monarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span state</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Music_and_performing_arts"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Music and performing arts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Science_and_technology"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Science and technology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See surveys</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Early_Ottomans"><span class="tocnumber">14.2</span> <span class="toctext">Early Ottomans</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Military_2"><span class="tocnumber">14.3</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Miscellaneous"><span class="tocnumber">14.4</span> <span class="toctext">Miscellaneous</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Historiography"><span class="tocnumber">14.5</span> <span class="toctext">Historiography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Names of the Ottoman Empire">Names of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<p>The word <i>Ottoman</i> is a historical <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisation</a> of the name of <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>, the founder of the Empire and of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty" title="Ottoman dynasty">House of Osman</a> (also known as the Ottoman dynasty). Osman\'s name in turn was the Turkish form of the Arabic name <i><a href="/wiki/Uthman_(name)" title="Uthman (name)">\xca\xbfUthm\xc4\x81n</a></i> (<span lang="ota-Arab" dir="rtl" title="Ottoman Turkish language text">\xd8\xb9\xd8\xab\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86</span>&#8206;). In <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>, the empire was referred to as <i>Devlet-i \xca\xbfAl\xc4\xabye-yi \xca\xbfO<u>s</u>m\xc4\x81n\xc4\xabye</i> (<span lang="ota-Arab" dir="rtl" title="Ottoman Turkish language text">\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xab\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xdb\x8c\xd9\x87</span>&#8206;),<sup id="cite_ref-twareekh.com_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twareekh.com-27">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> (literally "The Supreme Ottoman State") or alternatively <i>\xca\xbfO<u>s</u>m\xc4\x81nl\xc4\xb1 Devleti</i> (<span lang="ota-Arab" dir="rtl" title="Ottoman Turkish language text">\xd8\xb9\xd8\xab\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x89</span>&#8206;). In <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Modern Turkish</a>, it is known as <i>Osmanl\xc4\xb1 \xc4\xb0mparatorlu\xc4\x9fu</i> ("The Ottoman Empire") or <i>Osmanl\xc4\xb1 Devleti</i> ("The Ottoman State").\n</p><p>The Turkish word for "Ottoman" (<i>Osmanl\xc4\xb1</i>) originally referred to the tribal followers of Osman in the fourteenth century, and subsequently came to be used to refer to the empire\'s military-administrative elite. In contrast, the term "Turk" (<i>T\xc3\xbcrk</i>) was used to refer to the Anatolian peasant and tribal population, and was seen as a disparaging term when applied to urban, educated individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>, an educated urban-dwelling Turkish-speaker who was not a member of the military-administrative class would refer to himself neither as an <i>Osmanl\xc4\xb1</i> nor as a <i>T\xc3\xbcrk</i>, but rather as a <i>R\xc5\xabm\xc4\xab</i> (<span lang="ota-Arab" dir="rtl" title="Ottoman Turkish language text">\xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd9\x85\xd9\x89</span>&#8206;), or "Roman", meaning an inhabitant of the territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>. The term <i>R\xc5\xabm\xc4\xab</i> was also used to refer to Turkish-speakers by the other Muslim peoples of the empire and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Western Europe, the two names "Ottoman Empire" and "Turkey" were often used interchangeably, with "Turkey" being increasingly favoured both in formal and informal situations. This dichotomy was officially ended in 1920\xe2\x80\x9323, when the newly established Ankara-based Turkish government chose <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> as the sole official name. Most scholarly historians avoid the terms "Turkey", "Turks", and "Turkish" when referring to the Ottomans, due to the empire\'s multinational character.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="History of the Ottoman Empire">History of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire">Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Rise_.28c._1299.E2.80.931453.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_(c._1299\xe2\x80\x931453)">Rise (c. 1299\xe2\x80\x931453)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Rise of the Ottoman Empire">Rise of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty" title="Ottoman dynasty">Ottoman dynasty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza Thesis">Gaza Thesis</a></div>\n<p>As the Seljuk <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">Sultanate of Rum</a> declined in the 13th century, Anatolia was divided into a patchwork of independent Turkish principalities known as the <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_Beyliks" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatolian Beyliks">Anatolian Beyliks</a>. One of these beyliks, in the region of <a href="/wiki/Bithynia" title="Bithynia">Bithynia</a> on the frontier of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, was led by the Turkish tribal leader <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman</a> (d. 1323/4), a figure of obscure origins from whom the name Ottoman is derived.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Osman\'s early followers consisted both of Turkish tribal groups and Byzantine renegades, many but not all converts to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Osman extended the control of his principality by conquering <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> towns along the <a href="/wiki/Sakarya_River" title="Sakarya River">Sakarya River</a>. It is not well understood how the early Ottomans came to dominate their neighbours, due to the lack of sources surviving from this period. The <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza Thesis">Gaza Thesis</a> theory popular during the twentieth century credited their success to their rallying of religious warriors to fight for them in the name of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, but it is now highly criticised and no longer generally accepted by historians, and no consensus on the nature of the early Ottoman state\'s expansion has replaced it.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg" width="220" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2018" data-file-height="2943" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nicopolis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis" title="Battle of Nicopolis">Battle of Nicopolis</a> in 1396. Painting from 1523.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the century after the death of Osman I, Ottoman rule began to extend over Anatolia and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans" title="History of the Balkans">Balkans</a>. Osman\'s son, <a href="/wiki/Orhan" title="Orhan">Orhan</a>, captured the northwestern Anatolian city of <a href="/wiki/Bursa" title="Bursa">Bursa</a> in 1326, making it the new capital of the Ottoman state and supplanting Byzantine control in the region. The important port city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> was captured from the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetians</a> in 1387 and sacked. The Ottoman victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo" title="Battle of Kosovo">Kosovo in 1389</a> effectively marked <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Serbian_Empire" title="Fall of the Serbian Empire">the end of Serbian power</a> in the region, paving the way for Ottoman expansion into Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nicopolis" title="Battle of Nicopolis">Battle of Nicopolis</a> in 1396, widely regarded as the last large-scale <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">crusade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, failed to stop the advance of the victorious Ottoman Turks.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the Turks expanded into the Balkans, the <a href="/wiki/Sieges_of_Constantinople#Ottoman_Sieges" class="mw-redirect" title="Sieges of Constantinople">conquest of Constantinople</a> became a crucial objective. The Ottomans had already wrested control of nearly all former <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine lands</a> surrounding the city, but the heavy defence of Constantinople\'s strategic position on the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> Strait made it difficult to conquer. In 1402, the Byzantines were temporarily relieved when the <a href="/wiki/Turco-Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Turco-Mongol">Turco-Mongol</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>, invaded Ottoman Anatolia from the east. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara" title="Battle of Ankara">Battle of Ankara</a> in 1402, Timur defeated the Ottoman forces and took Sultan <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_I" title="Bayezid I">Bayezid I</a> as a prisoner, throwing the empire into disorder. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Interregnum" title="Ottoman Interregnum">ensuing civil war</a>, also known as the <i>Fetret Devri</i>, lasted from 1402 to 1413 as Bayezid\'s sons fought over succession. It ended when <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_I" title="Mehmed I">Mehmed I</a> emerged as the sultan and restored Ottoman power.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Balkan territories lost by the Ottomans after 1402, including Thessaloniki, Macedonia and Kosovo, were later recovered by <a href="/wiki/Murad_II" title="Murad II">Murad II</a> between the 1430s and 1450s. On 10 November 1444, Murad repelled the <a href="/wiki/Crusade_of_Varna" title="Crusade of Varna">Crusade of Varna</a> by defeating the Hungarian, Polish, and <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachian</a> armies under <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="W\xc5\x82adys\xc5\x82aw III of Poland">W\xc5\x82adys\xc5\x82aw III of Poland</a> (also King of Hungary) and <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Varna" title="Battle of Varna">Battle of Varna</a>, although Albanians under <a href="/wiki/Skanderbeg" title="Skanderbeg">Skanderbeg</a> continued to resist. Four years later, John Hunyadi prepared another army of Hungarian and Wallachian forces to attack the Turks, but was again defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kosovo_(1448)" title="Battle of Kosovo (1448)">Second Battle of Kosovo</a> in 1448.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Expansion_and_peak_.281453.E2.80.931566.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_and_peak_(1453\xe2\x80\x931566)">Expansion and peak (1453\xe2\x80\x931566)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Growth of the Ottoman Empire">Growth of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/220px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/330px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg/440px-Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg 2x" data-file-width="903" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zonaro_GatesofConst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Mehmed II</a>\'s entry into <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>; painting by <a href="/wiki/Fausto_Zonaro" title="Fausto Zonaro">Fausto Zonaro</a> (1854\xe2\x80\x931929)</div></div></div>\n<p>The son of Murad II, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a>, reorganized the state and the military, and conquered <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Constantinople</a> on 29 May 1453. Mehmed allowed the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a> to maintain its autonomy and land in exchange for accepting Ottoman authority.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google-37">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Because of bad relations between the states of western Europe and the later Byzantine Empire, the majority of the Orthodox population accepted Ottoman rule as preferable to Venetian rule.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google-37">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Albanian resistance was a major obstacle to Ottoman expansion on the Italian peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 15th and 16th centuries, the Ottoman Empire entered a <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Growth of the Ottoman Empire">period of expansion</a>. The Empire prospered under the rule of a line of committed and effective <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Dynasty">Sultans</a>. It also flourished economically due to its control of the major overland trade routes between Europe and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;note 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Selim_I" title="Selim I">Selim I</a> (1512\xe2\x80\x931520) dramatically expanded the Empire\'s eastern and southern frontiers by defeating <a href="/wiki/Ismail_I" title="Ismail I">Shah Ismail</a> of <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid</a> <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chaldiran" title="Battle of Chaldiran">Battle of Chaldiran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Selim I established <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ottoman_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Ottoman Egypt">Ottoman rule in Egypt</a>, and created a naval presence on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. After this Ottoman expansion, a competition started between the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and the Ottoman Empire to become the dominant power in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg/220px-Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg" width="220" height="361" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg/330px-Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg/440px-Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1856" data-file-height="3043" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Suleiman_I_after_the_victory_at_Moh%C3%A1cs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Moh\xc3\xa1cs">Battle of Moh\xc3\xa1cs</a> in 1526<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a> (1520\xe2\x80\x931566) captured <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> in 1521, conquered the southern and central parts of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Hungarian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman\xe2\x80\x93Hungarian Wars">Ottoman\xe2\x80\x93Hungarian Wars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and, after his historic victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Moh\xc3\xa1cs">Battle of Moh\xc3\xa1cs</a> in 1526, he established Turkish rule in the territory of present-day Hungary (except the western part) and other Central European territories. He then laid <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna" title="Siege of Vienna">siege to Vienna</a> in 1529, but failed to take the city.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 1532, he made another <a href="/wiki/Little_War_in_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Little War in Hungary">attack</a> on Vienna, but was repulsed in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_G%C3%BCns" title="Siege of G\xc3\xbcns">Siege of G\xc3\xbcns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson442_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson442-47">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-\xc3\x81goston_and_Alan_Masters583_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-\xc3\x81goston_and_Alan_Masters583-48">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and, intermittently, <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, became tributary principalities of the Ottoman Empire. In the east, the Ottoman Turks <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Safavid_War_(1532%E2%80%9355)" title="Ottoman\xe2\x80\x93Safavid War (1532\xe2\x80\x9355)">took</a> <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> from the Persians in 1535, gaining control of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and naval access to the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. In 1555, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> became officially partitioned for the first time between the Safavids and the Ottomans, a <i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo" title="Status quo">status quo</a></i> that would remain until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%9374)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768\xe2\x80\x9374)">Russo-Turkish War (1768\xe2\x80\x9374)</a>. By this partitioning of the Caucasus as signed in the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya" title="Peace of Amasya">Peace of Amasya</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Western_Armenia" title="Western Armenia">Western Armenia</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan" title="Kurdistan">Kurdistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti" title="Kingdom of Imereti">Western Georgia</a> (incl. western <a href="/wiki/Samtskhe-Atabagate" class="mw-redirect" title="Samtskhe-Atabagate">Samtskhe</a>) fell into Ottoman hands,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> while southern <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Armenia" title="Eastern Armenia">Eastern Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Georgia">Eastern Georgia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> remained Persian.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Preveza_(1538).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Preveza_%281538%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="499" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Preveza_(1538).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha">Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha</a> defeats the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1538)" title="Holy League (1538)">Holy League</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> under the command of <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Doria" title="Andrea Doria">Andrea Doria</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza" title="Battle of Preveza">Battle of Preveza</a> in 1538</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern France">France</a> and the Ottoman Empire, united by mutual opposition to <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> rule, became strong allies. The French conquests of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Nice" title="Siege of Nice">Nice</a> (1543) and <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Corsica_(1553)" title="Invasion of Corsica (1553)">Corsica</a> (1553) occurred as a joint venture between the forces of the French king <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> and Suleiman, and were commanded by the Ottoman admirals <a href="/wiki/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha">Barbarossa Hayreddin Pasha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turgut_Reis" class="mw-redirect" title="Turgut Reis">Turgut Reis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A month before the siege of Nice, France supported the Ottomans with an artillery unit during the 1543 Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Esztergom_(1543)" title="Siege of Esztergom (1543)">conquest of Esztergom</a> in northern Hungary. After further advances by the Turks, the Habsburg ruler <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand</a> officially recognized Ottoman ascendancy in Hungary in 1547.\n</p><p>By the end of Suleiman\'s reign, the Empire spanned approximately 877,888&#160;sq&#160;mi (2,273,720&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), extending over three continents.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the Empire became a dominant naval force, controlling much of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> By this time, the Ottoman Empire was a major part of the European political sphere. The success of its political and military establishment was compared to the Roman Empire, by the likes of Italian scholar <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Sansovino" title="Francesco Sansovino">Francesco Sansovino</a> and the French political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bodin" title="Jean Bodin">Jean Bodin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deringil709_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deringil709-54">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Stagnation_and_reform_.281566.E2.80.931827.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stagnation_and_reform_(1566\xe2\x80\x931827)">Stagnation and reform (1566\xe2\x80\x931827)</span></h3>\n<h4><span id="Revolts.2C_reversals.2C_and_revivals_.281566.E2.80.931683.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolts,_reversals,_and_revivals_(1566\xe2\x80\x931683)">Revolts, reversals, and revivals (1566\xe2\x80\x931683)</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transformation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Transformation of the Ottoman Empire">Transformation of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Decline_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Decline Thesis">Ottoman Decline Thesis</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article\'s <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Ottoman_Empire#The_Decline_Paradigm" title="Talk:Ottoman Empire">talk page</a>. Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(September 2016)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpire1566.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/OttomanEmpire1566.png/220px-OttomanEmpire1566.png" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/OttomanEmpire1566.png/330px-OttomanEmpire1566.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/OttomanEmpire1566.png/440px-OttomanEmpire1566.png 2x" data-file-width="3596" data-file-height="2581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OttomanEmpire1566.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The extent of the Ottoman Empire in 1566, upon the death of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Szigetvar_1566.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Szigetvar_1566.jpg/220px-Szigetvar_1566.jpg" width="220" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Szigetvar_1566.jpg/330px-Szigetvar_1566.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Szigetvar_1566.jpg/440px-Szigetvar_1566.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1272" data-file-height="1819" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Szigetvar_1566.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman miniature about the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Szigetv%C3%A1r" title="Siege of Szigetv\xc3\xa1r">Szigetv\xc3\xa1r campaign</a> showing Ottoman troops and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Tatars</a> as avant-garde</div></div></div>\n<p>In the second half of the sixteenth century the Ottoman Empire came under increasing strain from inflation and the rapidly rising costs of warfare that were impacting both Europe and the Middle East. These pressures led to a series of crises around the year 1600, placing great strain upon the Ottoman system of government.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The empire underwent a series of transformations of its political and military institutions in response to these challenges, enabling it to successfully adapt to the new conditions of the seventeenth century and remain powerful, militarily and economically.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Historians of the mid-twentieth century once characterized this period as one of stagnation and decline, but this view is now rejected by the majority of academics.<sup id="cite_ref-decline_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decline-20">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The discovery of new maritime trade routes by Western European states allowed them to avoid the Ottoman trade monopoly. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> in 1488 initiated <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_naval_expeditions_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Ottoman naval expeditions in the Indian Ocean">a series of Ottoman-Portuguese naval wars</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> throughout the 16th century. Despite the growing European presence in the Indian Ocean, Ottoman trade with the east continued to flourish. Cairo in particular benefitted from the rise of Yemeni coffee as a popular consumer commodity. As coffeehouses appeared in cities and towns across the empire, Cairo developed into a major center for its trade, contributing to its continued prosperity throughout the seventeenth and much of the eighteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under <a href="/wiki/Ivan_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan IV">Ivan IV</a> (1533\xe2\x80\x931584), the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a> expanded into the Volga and Caspian region at the expense of the Tatar khanates. In 1571, the Crimean khan <a href="/wiki/Devlet_I_Giray" title="Devlet I Giray">Devlet I Giray</a>, supported by the Ottomans, <a href="/wiki/Russo-Crimean_War_(1571)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Crimean War (1571)">burned Moscow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies2007_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2007-59">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The next year, the invasion was repeated but repelled at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi" title="Battle of Molodi">Battle of Molodi</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a> continued to invade Eastern Europe in a series of <a href="/wiki/Tatar_invasions" class="mw-redirect" title="Tatar invasions">slave raids</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Subtelny2000_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subtelny2000-60">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and remained a significant power in Eastern Europe until the end of the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In southern Europe, a <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">Catholic coalition</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> won a victory over the Ottoman fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> (1571). It was a startling, if mostly symbolic,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979272-62">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> blow to the image of Ottoman invincibility, an image which the victory of the Knights of Malta against the Ottoman invaders in the 1565 <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta" title="Great Siege of Malta">Siege of Malta</a> had recently set about eroding.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The battle was far more damaging to the Ottoman navy in sapping experienced manpower than the loss of ships, which were rapidly replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman navy recovered quickly, persuading Venice to sign a peace treaty in 1573, allowing the Ottomans to expand and consolidate their position in North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198067-65">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1341" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> in 1571</div></div></div>\n<p>By contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> frontier had settled somewhat, a stalemate caused by a stiffening of the Habsburg defences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198071-66">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Long_Turkish_War" title="Long Turkish War">Long War</a> against <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> Austria (1593\xe2\x80\x931606) created the need for greater numbers of Ottoman infantry equipped with firearms, resulting in a relaxation of recruitment policy. This contributed to problems of indiscipline and outright rebelliousness within the corps, which were never fully solved.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090\xe2\x80\x9392_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198090\xe2\x80\x9392-67">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsolete&#160;source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Irregular sharpshooters (<a href="/wiki/Sekban" title="Sekban">Sekban</a>) were also recruited, and on demobilization turned to <a href="/wiki/Brigandage" title="Brigandage">brigandage</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jelali_revolts" class="mw-redirect" title="Jelali revolts">Jelali revolts</a> (1590\xe2\x80\x931610), which engendered widespread anarchy in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in the late 16th and early 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> With the Empire\'s population reaching 30 million people by 1600, the shortage of land placed further pressure on the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979281-69">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="This claim needs references to more current sources. (September 2016)">obsolete&#160;source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In spite of these problems, the Ottoman state remained strong, and its army did not collapse or suffer crushing defeats. The only exceptions were campaigns against the <a href="/wiki/Safavid" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavid">Safavid</a> dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>, where many of the Ottoman eastern provinces were lost, some permanently. This <a href="/wiki/Ottoman-Safavid_War_(1603-1618)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman-Safavid War (1603-1618)">1603\xe2\x80\x931618</a> war eventually resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nasuh_Pasha" title="Treaty of Nasuh Pasha">Treaty of Nasuh Pasha</a>, which ceded the entire Caucasus, except westernmost Georgia, back into Iranian Safavid possession.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boksida,_karta_ur_Wr.110:5_(Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_(I.34.17)_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif.jpg" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Boksida%2C_karta_ur_Wr.110%3A5_%28Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_%28I.34.17%29_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4075" data-file-height="3425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boksida,_karta_ur_Wr.110:5_(Turc._Imper._Asia_Geographie_(I.34.17)_-_Skoklosters_slott_-_82210.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map from 1654</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/220px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/330px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg/440px-Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Battle_1683.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Second Siege of Vienna</a> in 1683</div></div></div>\n<p>During his brief majority reign, <a href="/wiki/Murad_IV" title="Murad IV">Murad IV</a> (1623\xe2\x80\x931640) reasserted central authority and recaptured <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (1639) from the <a href="/wiki/Safavids" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavids">Safavids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198073-71">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zuhab" title="Treaty of Zuhab">Treaty of Zuhab</a> of that same year decisively parted the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and adjacent regions between the two neighbouring empires as it had already been defined in the 1555 <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya" title="Peace of Amasya">Peace of Amasya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_women" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of women">Sultanate of women</a> (1623\xe2\x80\x931656) was a period in which the mothers of young sultans exercised power on behalf of their sons. The most prominent women of this period were <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6sem_Sultan" title="K\xc3\xb6sem Sultan">K\xc3\xb6sem Sultan</a> and her daughter-in-law <a href="/wiki/Turhan_Hatice" class="mw-redirect" title="Turhan Hatice">Turhan Hatice</a>, whose political rivalry culminated in K\xc3\xb6sem\'s murder in 1651.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074\xe2\x80\x9375_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198074\xe2\x80\x9375-74">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6pr%C3%BCl%C3%BC_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="K\xc3\xb6pr\xc3\xbcl\xc3\xbc Era">K\xc3\xb6pr\xc3\xbcl\xc3\xbc Era</a> (1656\xe2\x80\x931703), effective control of the Empire was exercised by a sequence of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Viziers</a> from the K\xc3\xb6pr\xc3\xbcl\xc3\xbc family. The K\xc3\xb6pr\xc3\xbcl\xc3\xbc Vizierate saw renewed military success with authority restored in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, the conquest of <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a> completed in 1669, and expansion into Polish southern <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, with the strongholds of <a href="/wiki/Khotyn" title="Khotyn">Khotyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kamianets-Podilskyi" title="Kamianets-Podilskyi">Kamianets-Podilskyi</a> and the territory of <a href="/wiki/Podolia" title="Podolia">Podolia</a> ceding to Ottoman control in 1676.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080\xe2\x80\x9381_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198080\xe2\x80\x9381-75">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This period of renewed assertiveness came to a calamitous end in 1683 when Grand Vizier <a href="/wiki/Kara_Mustafa_Pasha" title="Kara Mustafa Pasha">Kara Mustafa Pasha</a> led a huge army to attempt a second Ottoman siege of <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Great Turkish War</a> of 1683\xe2\x80\x931699. The final assault being fatally delayed, the Ottoman forces were swept away by allied Habsburg, German and Polish forces spearheaded by the Polish king <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Battle of Vienna</a>. The alliance of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1684)" title="Holy League (1684)">Holy League</a> pressed home the advantage of the defeat at Vienna, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz" title="Treaty of Karlowitz">Treaty of Karlowitz</a> (26 January 1699), which ended the Great Turkish War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979357-76">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The Ottomans surrendered control of significant territories, many permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198084-77">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_II" title="Mustafa II">Mustafa II</a> (1695\xe2\x80\x931703) led the counterattack of 1695\xe2\x80\x9396 against the Habsburgs in Hungary, but was undone at the disastrous defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zenta" title="Battle of Zenta">Zenta</a> (in modern Serbia), 11 September 1697.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083\xe2\x80\x9384_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198083\xe2\x80\x9384-78">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_threat_grows">Russian threat grows</span></h4>\n<p>Aside from the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">Banat</a> and the temporary loss of <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (1717\xe2\x80\x9339), the Ottoman border on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> remained stable during the eighteenth century. <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Russia_1500%E2%80%931800" title="Expansion of Russia 1500\xe2\x80\x931800">Russian expansion</a>, however, presented a large and growing threat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-79">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Accordingly, King <a href="/wiki/Charles_XII_of_Sweden" title="Charles XII of Sweden">Charles XII of Sweden</a> was welcomed as an ally in the Ottoman Empire following his defeat by the Russians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Poltava" title="Battle of Poltava">Battle of Poltava</a> of 1709 in central Ukraine (part of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> of 1700\xe2\x80\x931721).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979371-79">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Charles XII persuaded the Ottoman Sultan <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_III" title="Ahmed III">Ahmed III</a> to declare war on Russia, which resulted in an Ottoman victory in the <a href="/wiki/Pruth_River_Campaign" title="Pruth River Campaign">Pruth River Campaign</a> of 1710\xe2\x80\x931711, in Moldavia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979372-80">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/220px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/330px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG/440px-1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1720_Huchtenburg_Eroberungs_Belgrads_1717_anagoria.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Austrian troops led by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Eugene_of_Savoy" title="Prince Eugene of Savoy">Prince Eugene of Savoy</a> capture <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> in 1717</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_of_1716%E2%80%931718" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Turkish War of 1716\xe2\x80\x931718">Austro-Turkish War of 1716\xe2\x80\x931718</a> the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Passarowitz" title="Treaty of Passarowitz">Treaty of Passarowitz</a> confirmed the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">Banat</a>, Serbia and <a href="/wiki/Oltenia" title="Oltenia">"Little Walachia" (Oltenia)</a> to Austria. The Treaty also revealed that the Ottoman Empire was on the defensive and unlikely to present any further aggression in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979376-81">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%931739)" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Russian\xe2\x80\x93Turkish War (1735\xe2\x80\x931739)">Austro-Russian\xe2\x80\x93Turkish War</a> (1735\xe2\x80\x931739), which was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Belgrade" title="Treaty of Belgrade">Treaty of Belgrade</a> in 1739, resulted in the recovery of Serbia and Oltenia, but the Empire lost the port of <a href="/wiki/Azov" title="Azov">Azov</a>, north of the Crimean Peninsula, to the Russians. After this treaty the Ottoman Empire was able to enjoy a generation of peace, as Austria and Russia were forced to deal with the rise of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979392-82">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Science_and_Technology_in_the_Ottoman_Empire#Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Science and Technology in the Ottoman Empire">Educational and technological reforms</a> came about, including the establishment of higher education institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University" title="Istanbul Technical University">Istanbul Technical University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 1734 an artillery school was established to impart Western-style artillery methods, but the Islamic clergy successfully objected under the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Theodicy" title="Theodicy">theodicy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-84">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 1754 the artillery school was reopened on a semi-secret basis.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-84">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 1726, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Muteferrika" title="Ibrahim Muteferrika">Ibrahim Muteferrika</a> convinced the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a> <a href="/wiki/Nev%C5%9Fehirli_Damat_%C4%B0brahim_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Nev\xc5\x9fehirli Damat \xc4\xb0brahim Pasha">Nev\xc5\x9fehirli Damat \xc4\xb0brahim Pasha</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Mufti" title="Grand Mufti">Grand Mufti</a>, and the clergy on the efficiency of the printing press, and Muteferrika was later granted by Sultan Ahmed III permission to publish non-religious books (despite opposition from some <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calligraphy" title="Islamic calligraphy">calligraphers</a> and religious leaders).<sup id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-katip_celebi-85">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Muteferrika\'s press published its first book in 1729 and, by 1743, issued 17 works in 23 volumes, each having between 500 and 1,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-katip_celebi_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-katip_celebi-85">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-watson_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watson-86">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/220px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/330px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg/440px-January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1130" data-file-height="754" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:January_Suchodolski_-_Ochakiv_siege.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman troops attempt to halt advancing Russians during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Ochakov_(1788)" title="Siege of Ochakov (1788)">Siege of Ochakov</a> in 1788.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1768 Russian-backed Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Haidamaka" title="Haidamaka">Haidamakas</a>, pursuing Polish confederates, entered <a href="/wiki/Balta,_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Balta, Ukraine">Balta</a>, an Ottoman-controlled town on the border of Bessarabia in Ukraine, and massacred its citizens and burned the town to the ground. This action provoked the Ottoman Empire into the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768\xe2\x80\x931774)">Russo-Turkish War of 1768\xe2\x80\x931774</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca" title="Treaty of K\xc3\xbc\xc3\xa7\xc3\xbck Kaynarca">Treaty of K\xc3\xbc\xc3\xa7\xc3\xbck Kaynarca</a> of 1774 ended the war and provided freedom to worship for the Christian citizens of the Ottoman-controlled provinces of Wallachia and Moldavia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinross1979405-87">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> By the late 18th century, after a number of defeats in the wars with Russia, some people in the Ottoman Empire began to conclude that the reforms of <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> had given the Russians an edge, and the Ottomans would have to keep up with Western technology in order to avoid further defeats.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_a_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_a-84">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> (1789\xe2\x80\x931807) made the first major attempts to <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_military_reform_efforts" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman military reform efforts">modernize the army</a>, but his reforms were hampered by the religious leadership and the <a href="/wiki/Janissary" class="mw-redirect" title="Janissary">Janissary</a> corps. Jealous of their privileges and firmly opposed to change, the Janissary <a href="/wiki/Janissary_revolts" class="mw-redirect" title="Janissary revolts">revolted</a>. Selim\'s efforts cost him his throne and his life, but were resolved in spectacular and bloody fashion by his successor, the dynamic <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_II" title="Mahmud II">Mahmud II</a>, who <a href="/wiki/The_Auspicious_Incident" class="mw-redirect" title="The Auspicious Incident">eliminated the Janissary corps</a> in 1826.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_(1789).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/220px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/330px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg/440px-Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_%281789%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2311" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Sultan_Selim_III_(1789).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> receiving dignitaries during an audience at the Gate of Felicity, <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Serbian_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbian revolution">Serbian revolution</a> (1804\xe2\x80\x931815) marked the beginning of an era of <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire">national awakening</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">Eastern Question</a>. In 1811, the fundamentalist Wahhabis of Arabia, led by the al-Saud family revolted against the Ottomans. Unable to defeat the Wahhabi rebels, the Sublime Porte had Mohammad Ali the Great, the <i>vali</i> (governor) of Egypt tasked with retaking Arabia which ended with the destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Diriyah" title="Emirate of Diriyah">Emirate of Diriyah</a> in 1818. The <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">Suzerainty</a> of Serbia as a hereditary monarchy under its own <a href="/wiki/Obrenovi%C4%87_dynasty" title="Obrenovi\xc4\x87 dynasty">dynasty</a> was acknowledged <i>de jure</i> in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Berend2003_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berend2003-89">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In 1821, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Greece" title="Ottoman Greece">Greeks</a> <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">declared war</a> on the Sultan. A rebellion that originated in Moldavia as a diversion was followed by the main revolution in the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a>, which, along with the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Corinth" title="Gulf of Corinth">Gulf of Corinth</a>, became the first parts of the Ottoman Empire to achieve independence (in 1829). In 1830, the French invaded Algeria, which was lost to the empire. In 1831, Mohammad Ali revolted with the aim of making himself sultan and founding a new dynasty, and his French-trained army under his son Ibrahim Pasha defeated the Ottoman Army as it marched on Constantinople, coming within 200 miles of the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In desperation, the Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_II" title="Mahmud II">Mahmud II</a> appealed to the empire\'s traditional archenemy Russia for help, asking the Emperor Nicholas I to send an expeditionary force to save him.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In return for signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_H%C3%BCnk%C3%A2r_%C4%B0skelesi" title="Treaty of H\xc3\xbcnk\xc3\xa2r \xc4\xb0skelesi">Treaty of H\xc3\xbcnk\xc3\xa2r \xc4\xb0skelesi</a>, the Russians sent the expeditionary force, which deterred Ibrahim from taking Constantinople.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Under the terms of Peace of Kutahia, signed on 5 May 1833 Mohammad Ali agreed to abandon his claim to the throne, in exchange for which he was made the <i>vali</i> of the <i>vilayets</i> (provinces) of Crete, Aleppo, Tripoli, Damascus and Sidon (the latter four comprising modern Syria and Lebanon), and given the right to collect taxes in Adana.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Had it not been for the Russian intervention, it is almost certain Mahumd II would have been overthrown and Mohammad Ali would have become the new sultan, marking the beginning of a recurring pattern where the Sublime Porte needed the help of outsiders to save itself.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg/220px-%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg/330px-%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg/440px-%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%CE%97_%CE%BC%CE%AC%CF%87%CE%B7_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%91%CE%BB%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AC%CE%BD%CE%B1%CF%82.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a> (1821\xe2\x80\x931829) against the Ottomans</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1839, the Sublime Porte attempted to take back what it lost to the de facto independent <i>vilayet</i> of Egypt, and suffered a crushing defeat, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Crisis_of_1840" title="Oriental Crisis of 1840">Oriental Crisis</a> as Mohammad Ali was very close to France, and the prospect of him as Sultan was widely viewed as putting the entire empire into the French sphere of influence.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As the Sublime Porte had proved itself incapable of defeating the Egyptians, Britain and Austria intervened to defeat Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96_91-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karsh,_Effraim_page_96-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> By the mid-19th century, the Ottoman Empire was called the <a href="/wiki/Sick_man_of_Europe" title="Sick man of Europe">"sick man"</a> by Europeans. The <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerain states</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Principality of Serbia</a>, Wallachia and <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> \xe2\x80\x93 moved towards <i>de jure</i> independence during the 1860s and 1870s.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Decline_and_modernization_.281828.E2.80.931908.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_and_modernization_(1828\xe2\x80\x931908)">Decline and modernization (1828\xe2\x80\x931908)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of the Ottoman Empire">Decline of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a> period (1839\xe2\x80\x931876), the government\'s series of constitutional reforms led to a fairly modern <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Conscription in the Ottoman Empire">conscripted army</a>, banking system reforms, the decriminalization of homosexuality, the replacement of religious law with secular law<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guilds</a> with modern factories. The Ottoman Ministry of Post was established in Istanbul on 23 October 1840.<sup id="cite_ref-PTT_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT-94">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PTT2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PTT2-95">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Morse" title="Samuel Morse">Samuel Morse</a> received a Turkish <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Telegraphy" title="Telegraphy">telegraph</a> in 1847, which was issued by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd\xc3\xbclmecid I">Abd\xc3\xbclmecid</a> who personally tested the new invention.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Following this successful test, work on the first Turkish telegraph line (Istanbul-<a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>-<a href="/wiki/%C5%9Eumnu" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc5\x9eumnu">\xc5\x9eumnu</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-NTVtarih2_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTVtarih2-97">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> began on 9 August 1847.<sup id="cite_ref-telekomhistory_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telekomhistory-98">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The reformist period peaked with the Constitution, called the <i><a href="/wiki/Kan%C3%BBn-u_Es%C3%A2s%C3%AE" class="mw-redirect" title="Kan\xc3\xbbn-u Es\xc3\xa2s\xc3\xae">Kan\xc3\xbbn-u Es\xc3\xa2s\xc3\xae</a></i>. The empire\'s <a href="/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era_(Ottoman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Constitutional Era (Ottoman Empire)">First Constitutional era</a> was short-lived. The parliament survived for only two years before the sultan suspended it.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg/220px-Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg/330px-Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg/440px-Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_at_river_Skit_1877.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" title="United Principalities">Romania</a>, fighting on the Russian side, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_War_of_Independence" title="Romanian War of Independence">gained independence</a> from the Ottoman Empire in 1878 after the end of <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x931878)">Russo-Turkish War</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Christian population of the empire, owing to their higher educational levels, started to pull ahead of the Muslim majority, leading to much resentment on the part of the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_b-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 1861, there were 571 primary and 94 secondary schools for Ottoman Christians with 140,000 pupils in total, a figure that vastly exceeded the number of Muslim children in school at the same time, who were further hindered by the amount of time spent learning Arabic and Islamic theology.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_b-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Stone further suggested that the Arabic alphabet, which Turkish was written in until
