1928, was very ill-suited to reflect the sounds of the Turkish language (which is a Turkic as opposed to Semitic language), which imposed a further difficulty on Turkish children.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_b-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In turn, the higher educational levels of the Christians allowed them to play a larger role in the economy, with the rise in prominence of groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Sursock_family" title="Sursock family">Sursock family</a> indicative of this shift in influence. <sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_b-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 1911, of the 654 wholesale companies in Istanbul, 528 were owned by ethnic Greeks.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google_b_99-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google_b-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In many cases, Christians and also Jews were able to gain protection from European consuls and citizenship, meaning they were protected from Ottoman law and not subject to the same economic regulations as their Muslim comrades.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg/170px-Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg/255px-Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg/340px-Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="2026" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Konstantin_Makovsky_-_The_Bulgarian_martyresses.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Bulgarian martyresses</i> (1877) by <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Makovsky" title="Konstantin Makovsky">Konstantin Makovsky</a>, a Russian propaganda painting which depicts the rape of Bulgarian women by the <a href="/wiki/Bashi-bazouk" title="Bashi-bazouk">bashi-bazouks</a> during the <a href="/wiki/April_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="April Uprising">April Uprising</a>, with the purpose of mobilizing public support for the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)">Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Unrestrained by the laws that governed regular soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Army">Ottoman Army</a>, the bashi-bazouks became notorious for preying on civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> (1853\xe2\x80\x931856) was part of a long-running contest between the major European powers for influence over territories of the <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of the Ottoman Empire">declining Ottoman Empire</a>. The financial burden of the war led the Ottoman state to issue <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_public_debt" title="Ottoman public debt">foreign loans</a> amounting to 5 million pounds sterling on 4 August 1854.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The war caused an exodus of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, about 200,000 of whom moved to the Ottoman Empire in continuing waves of emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Toward the end of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian Wars">Caucasian Wars</a>, 90% of the <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a> were <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic cleansing of Circassians">ethnically cleansed</a><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and exiled from their homelands in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and fled to the Ottoman Empire,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> resulting in the settlement of 500,000 to 700,000 Circassians in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-Jaimoukha2001_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jaimoukha2001-110">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2013)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hille2010_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hille2010-111">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChirotMcCauley2010_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChirotMcCauley2010-112">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Some Circassian organisations give much higher numbers, totaling 1\xe2\x80\x931.5 million deported or killed. Crimean Tartar refugees in the late 19th century played an especially notable role in seeking to modernize Ottoman education and in first promoting both Pan-Turkicism and a sense of Turkish nationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-113">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In this period, the Ottoman Empire spent only small amounts of public funds on education; for example in 1860\xe2\x80\x9361 only 0.2 per cent of the total budget was invested in education.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\nAs the Ottoman state attempted to modernize its infrastructure and army in response to threats from the outside, it also opened itself up to a different kind of threat: that of creditors. Indeed, as the historian Eugene Rogan has written, "the single greatest threat to the independence of the Middle East" in the nineteenth century "was not the armies of Europe but its banks."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman state, which had begun taking on debt with the Crimean War, was forced to declare bankruptcy in 1875.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-116">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> By 1881, the Ottoman Empire agreed to have its debt controlled by an institution known as the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Public_Debt_Administration" title="Ottoman Public Debt Administration">Ottoman Public Debt Administration</a>, a council of European men with presidency alternating between France and Britain. The body controlled swaths of the Ottoman economy, and used its position to ensure that European capital continued to penetrate the empire, often to the detriment of local Ottoman interests.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-116">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Bashi-bazouk" title="Bashi-bazouk">bashi-bazouks</a> brutally suppressed the <a href="/wiki/April_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="April Uprising">Bulgarian uprising</a> of 1876, massacring up to 100,000 people in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)">Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)</a> ended with a decisive victory for Russia. As a result, Ottoman holdings in Europe declined sharply: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Bulgaria" title="Principality of Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> was established as an independent principality inside the Ottoman Empire; <a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" title="United Principalities">Romania</a> achieved full independence; and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Serbia" title="History of Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> finally gained complete independence, but with smaller territories. In 1878, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> unilaterally occupied the Ottoman provinces of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_Vilayet" title="Bosnia Vilayet">Bosnia-Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Novi_Pazar" title="Sanjak of Novi Pazar">Novi Pazar</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> advocated for restoring the Ottoman territories on the Balkan Peninsula during the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a>, and in return Britain assumed the administration of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Britain later sent troops to <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in 1882 to put down the <a href="/wiki/Urabi_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Urabi Revolt">Urabi Revolt</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid II</a> was too paranoid to mobilize his own army, fearing this would result in a coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat \xe2\x80\x93 effectively gaining control in both territories. Abdul Hamid II, popularly known as "Abdul Hamid the Damned" on the account of his cruelty and paranoia, was so fearful of the threat of a coup that he did not allow his army to conduct war games, lest this serve as the cover for a coup, but he did see the need for military mobilization. In 1883, a German military mission under General Baron <a href="/wiki/Colmar_Freiherr_von_der_Goltz" title="Colmar Freiherr von der Goltz">Colmar von der Goltz</a> arrived to train the Ottoman Army, leading to the so-called "Goltz generation" of German-trained officers who were to play a notable role in the politics of the last years of the empire.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1894 to 1896, between 100,000 and 300,000 Armenians living throughout the empire were killed in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Hamidian_massacres" title="Hamidian massacres">Hamidian massacres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the Ottoman Empire gradually shrank in size, some 7\xe2\x80\x939 million Muslims from its former territories in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> islands migrated to <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Thrace" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Thrace">Eastern Thrace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Karpat2004_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karpat2004-121">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> After the Empire lost the <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">First Balkan War</a> (1912\xe2\x80\x9313), it lost all its <a href="/wiki/Balkan_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan peninsula">Balkan</a> territories except <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a> (European Turkey). This resulted in around 400,000 Muslims fleeing with the retreating Ottoman armies (with many dying from cholera brought by the soldiers), and with some 400,000 non-Muslims fleeing territory still under Ottoman rule.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Justin_McCarthy_(American_historian)" title="Justin McCarthy (American historian)">Justin McCarthy</a> estimates that during the period 1821 to 1922 several million Muslims died in the Balkans, with the expulsion of a similar number.<sup id="cite_ref-McCarthy1995_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCarthy1995-123">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carmichael2012_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carmichael2012-124">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buturovic2010_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buturovic2010-125">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 208px"><div style="width: 208px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 206px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="gallerybox" style="width: 339.33333333333px"><div style="width: 339.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 337.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a The <a href="/wiki/First_Constitutional_Era_(Ottoman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Constitutional Era (Ottoman Empire)">First Constitutional Era</a> lasted for only two years until 1878. The Ottoman Constitution and Parliament were <a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era_(Ottoman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Constitutional Era (Ottoman Empire)">restored 30 years later</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 171.33333333333px"><div style="width: 171.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 169.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1853\xe2\x80\x931856\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 218px"><div style="width: src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg/324px-The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg" width="216" height="130" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg/487px-The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg/649px-The_ruined_gateway_of_Prince_Eugene%2C_Belgrade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="462" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, c. 1865. In 1867, <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">France</a> forced the Ottoman military to retreat from northern <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, securing its <i>de facto</i> independence (formalized after the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)">Russo-Turkish War of 1877\xe2\x80\x9378</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> in 1878.)\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="Defeat_and_dissolution_.281908.E2.80.931922.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Defeat_and_dissolution_(1908\xe2\x80\x931922)">Defeat and dissolution (1908\xe2\x80\x931922)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Defeat_and_dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">Defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_during_World_War_I" title="History of the Ottoman Empire during World War I">History of the Ottoman Empire during World War I</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Le_Petir_Journal,_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg/180px-Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg" width="180" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg/270px-Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg/360px-Le_Petir_Journal%2C_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg 2x" data-file-width="732" data-file-height="1060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Le_Petir_Journal,_Proclamation_of_Mehmed_V.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mehmed_V" title="Mehmed V">Mehmed V</a> was proclaimed Sultan of the Ottoman Empire after the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Defeat_and_dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire</a> (1908\xe2\x80\x931922) began with the <a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era" title="Second Constitutional Era">Second Constitutional Era</a>, a moment of hope and promise established with the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a>. It restored the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_constitution_of_1876" title="Ottoman constitution of 1876">Ottoman constitution of 1876</a> and brought in <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="List of political parties in the Ottoman Empire">multi-party politics</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Elections in the Ottoman Empire">two-stage electoral system</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_electoral_law" title="Ottoman electoral law">electoral law</a>) under the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="General Assembly of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman parliament</a>. The constitution offered hope by freeing the empire\xe2\x80\x99s citizens to modernize the state\xe2\x80\x99s institutions, rejuvenate its strength, and enable it to hold its own against outside powers. Its guarantee of liberties promised to dissolve inter-communal tensions and transform the empire into a more harmonious place.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Instead, this period became the story of the twilight struggle of the Empire.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/200px-Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/300px-Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png/400px-Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png 2x" data-file-width="587" data-file-height="393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_the_1908_Revolution_in_Ottoman_Empire.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Declaration of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> by the leaders of the Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Millet (Ottoman Empire)">millets</a> in 1908</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultanvahideddin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sultanvahideddin.jpg/200px-Sultanvahideddin.jpg" width="200" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sultanvahideddin.jpg/300px-Sultanvahideddin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sultanvahideddin.jpg/400px-Sultanvahideddin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="521" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultanvahideddin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a>, the last Sultan of the Ottoman Empire, leaving the country after the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of the Ottoman Sultanate">abolition of the Ottoman sultanate</a>, 17 November 1922</div></div></div>\n<p>Members of <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">Young Turks</a> movement who had once gone underground now established their parties.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Among them \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a>,\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Freedom_and_Accord_Party" title="Freedom and Accord Party">Freedom and Accord Party</a>\xe2\x80\x9d were major parties. On the other end of the spectrum were ethnic parties which included <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party_in_Palestine_(Poale_Zion)" title="Jewish Social Democratic Labour Party in Palestine (Poale Zion)">Poale Zion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Fatat" title="Al-Fatat">Al-Fatat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_national_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian national movement">Armenian national movement</a> organized under <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Armenian Revolutionary Federation</a>. Profiting from the civil strife, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> officially annexed <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> in 1908. The last of the <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Census in the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman censuses</a> was performed in <a href="/wiki/1914_population_statistics_for_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="1914 population statistics for the Ottoman Empire">1914</a>. Despite <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_military_reforms" title="Ottoman military reforms">military reforms</a> which reconstituted the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Modern_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Modern Army">Ottoman Modern Army</a>, the Empire lost its North African territories and the Dodecanese in the <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">Italo-Turkish War</a> (1911) and almost all of its European territories in the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> (1912\xe2\x80\x931913). The Empire faced continuous unrest in the years leading up to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_countercoup_of_1909" title="Ottoman countercoup of 1909">Ottoman countercoup of 1909</a>, the <a href="/wiki/31_March_Incident" title="31 March Incident">31 March Incident</a> and two further coups in <a href="/wiki/1912_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1912 Ottoman coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">1912</a> and <a href="/wiki/1913_Ottoman_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1913 Ottoman coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">1913</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_during_World_War_I" title="History of the Ottoman Empire during World War I">history of the Ottoman Empire during World War I</a> began with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_entry_into_World_War_I" title="Ottoman entry into World War I">Ottoman surprise attack</a> on the Russian Black Sea coast on 29 October 1914. Following the attack, Russia and its allies, France and Britain, declared war on the Ottomans. There were several important Ottoman victories in the early years of the war, such as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gallipoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Gallipoli">Battle of Gallipoli</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kut" title="Siege of Kut">Siege of Kut</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthau336.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/220px-Morgenthau336.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/330px-Morgenthau336.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/440px-Morgenthau336.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3999" data-file-height="2731" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthau336.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a> was the Ottoman government\'s systematic extermination of its Armenian subjects. An estimated 1.5 million people were killed.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1915 the Ottoman government started the extermination of its ethnic Armenian population, resulting in the death of approximately 1.5 million Armenians in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The genocide was carried out during and after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and implemented in two phases: the wholesale killing of the able-bodied male population through massacre and subjection of army conscripts to forced labor, followed by the deportation of women, children, the elderly and infirm on <a href="/wiki/Death_march" title="Death march">death marches</a> leading to the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian desert">Syrian desert</a>. Driven forward by military escorts, the deportees were deprived of food and water and subjected to periodic robbery, rape, and systematic massacre.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Large-scale massacres were also committed against the Empire\'s <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_genocide" title="Assyrian genocide">Assyrian</a> minorities as part of the same campaign of ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Revolt" title="Arab Revolt">Arab Revolt</a> began in 1916 and turned the tide against the Ottomans on the Middle Eastern front, where they seemed to have the upper hand during the first two years of the war. The <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Mudros" title="Armistice of Mudros">Armistice of Mudros</a> was signed on 30 October 1918, setting the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partition of the Ottoman Empire">partition of the Ottoman Empire</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of S\xc3\xa8vres">Treaty of S\xc3\xa8vres</a>. This treaty, as designed in the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_London_(1920)" title="Conference of London (1920)">conference of London</a>, allowed the Sultan to retain his position and title. The <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Constantinople" title="Occupation of Constantinople">occupation of Constantinople</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_%C4%B0zmir" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of \xc4\xb0zmir">\xc4\xb0zmir</a> led to the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Turkish_national_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish national movement">Turkish national movement</a>, which won the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> (1919\xe2\x80\x9323) under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atat\xc3\xbcrk">Mustafa Kemal</a> (later given the surname "Atat\xc3\xbcrk"). The <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_the_Ottoman_Sultanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of the Ottoman Sultanate">sultanate was abolished</a> on 1 November 1922, and the last sultan, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a> (reigned 1918\xe2\x80\x9322), left the country on 17 November 1922. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">caliphate</a> was abolished on 3 March 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-Ozoglu_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ozoglu-133">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_debate_on_the_origins_and_nature_of_the_Ottoman_state">Historical debate on the origins and nature of the Ottoman state</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Thesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza Thesis">Gaza Thesis</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely on a single <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">source</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Ottoman_Empire##" title="Talk:Ottoman Empire">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ottoman_Empire&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span>  <small><i>(May 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Several historians such as British historian <a href="/wiki/Edward_Gibbon" title="Edward Gibbon">Edward Gibbon</a> and the Greek historian Dimitri Kitzikis have argued that after the fall of Constantinople, the Ottoman state took over the machinery of the Roman state, and that in essence the Ottoman Empire was a continuation of the Eastern Roman Empire under a thin Turkish Islamic guise.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Kitzikis called the Ottoman state "a Greek-Turkish condominium".<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_pages_86-100_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_pages_86-100-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The American historian <a href="/wiki/Speros_Vryonis" title="Speros Vryonis">Speros Vryonis</a> wrote that the Ottoman state was centered on "a Byzantine-Balkan base with a veneer of the Turkish language and the Islamic religion".<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_pages_86-100_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_pages_86-100-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Other historians have followed the lead of the Austrian historian <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wittek" title="Paul Wittek">Paul Wittek</a> who emphasized the Islamic character of the Ottoman state, seeing the Ottoman state as a "Jihad state" dedicated to expanding the world of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_pages_86-100_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_pages_86-100-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Another group of historians led by the Turkish historian M. Fuat Koprulu championed the "<i><a href="/wiki/Ghazi_(warrior)" title="Ghazi (warrior)">gazi</a></i> thesis" that saw the Ottoman state as a continuation of the way of life of the <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic tribes</a> who had come from East Asia to Anatolia via Central Asia and the Middle East on a much larger scale, and argued that the most important cultural influences on the Ottoman state came from Persia.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_pages_86-100_135-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_pages_86-100-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> More recently, the American historian <a href="/wiki/Heath_Lowry" class="mw-redirect" title="Heath Lowry">Heath Lowry</a> called the Ottoman state a "predatory confederacy" led in equal parts by Turks and Greeks converted to Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_pages_86-100_135-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_pages_86-100-135">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The British historian <a href="/wiki/Norman_Stone" title="Norman Stone">Norman Stone</a> suggested many continuities between the Eastern Roman and Ottoman empires such as the <i>zeugarion</i> tax of Byzantium becoming the Ottoman <i>Resm-i \xc3\xa7ift</i> tax, the <i><a href="/wiki/Pronoia" title="Pronoia">pronoia</a></i> land-holding system that linked the amount of land one owned with one\'s ability to raise cavalry becoming the Ottoman <i><a href="/wiki/Timar" title="Timar">timar</a></i> system, and the Ottoman measurement for land the <i>donum</i> was the same as the Byzantine <i>stremma</i>. Stone also pointed out that despite the fact that Sunni Islam was the state religion, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> was supported and controlled by the Ottoman state, and in return to accepting that control became the largest land-holder in the Ottoman Empire. Despite the similarities, Stone argued that a crucial difference was that the land grants under the <i>timar</i> system were not hereditary at first. Even after land grants under the <i>timar</i> system became inheritable, land ownings in the Ottoman Empire remained highly insecure, and the sultan could and did revoke land grants whenever he wished.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Stone argued this insecurity in land tenure strongly discouraged <i><a href="/wiki/Timariot" class="mw-redirect" title="Timariot">Timariots</a></i> from seeking long-term development of their land, and instead led the <i>timariots</i> to adopt a strategy of short term exploitation, which ultimately had deleterious effects on the Ottoman economy.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="State organisation of the Ottoman Empire">State organisation of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3554" data-file-height="2630" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Baptiste_Vanmour_-_Dinner_at_the_Palace_in_Honour_of_an_Ambassador_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ambassadors at the <a href="/wiki/Topkap%C4%B1_Palace" title="Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace">Topkap\xc4\xb1 Palace</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Before the reforms of the 19th and 20th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/State_organisation_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="State organisation of the Ottoman Empire">state organisation of the Ottoman Empire</a> was a system with two main dimensions, the military administration and the civil administration. The Sultan was the highest position in the system. The civil system was based on local administrative units based on the region\'s characteristics. The state had control over the clergy. Certain pre-Islamic Turkish traditions that had survived the adoption of administrative and legal practices from Islamic <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> remained important in Ottoman administrative circles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEItzkowitz198038-137">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> According to Ottoman understanding, the state\'s primary responsibility was to defend and extend the land of the Muslims and to ensure security and harmony within its borders in the overarching context of <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">orthodox</a> Islamic practice and dynastic sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-Kapucu_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kapucu-138">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ottoman Empire, or as a dynastic institution, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_dynasty" title="Ottoman dynasty">House of Osman</a>, was unprecedented and unequaled in the Islamic world for its size and duration.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In Europe, only the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> had a similarly unbroken line of sovereigns (kings/emperors) from the same family who ruled for so long, and during the same period, between the late 13th and early 20th centuries. The Ottoman dynasty was Turkish in origin. On eleven occasions, the sultan was deposed (replaced by another sultan of the Ottoman dynasty, who were either the former sultan\'s brother, son or nephew) because he was perceived by his enemies as a threat to the state. There were only two attempts in Ottoman history to unseat the ruling Ottoman dynasty, both failures, which suggests a political system that for an extended period was able to manage its revolutions without unnecessary instability.<sup id="cite_ref-Kapucu_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kapucu-138">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> As such, the last Ottoman sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a> (r. 1918\xe2\x80\x931922) was a <a href="/wiki/List_of_sultans_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="List of sultans of the Ottoman Empire">direct patrilineal (male-line) descendant</a> of the first Ottoman sultan <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a> (d. 1323/4), which was unparallelled in both Europe (e.g. the male line of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> became extinct in 1740) and in the Islamic world. The primary purpose of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Harem" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Harem">Imperial Harem</a> was to ensure the birth of male heirs to the Ottoman throne and secure the continuation of the direct patrilineal (male-line) descendance of the Ottoman sultans.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_allom,_c1840,_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png/220px-Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png/330px-Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png/440px-Thomas_allom%2C_c1840%2C_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="537" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_allom,_c1840,_The_Enterance_to_Divan.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>B\xc3\xa2b-\xc4\xb1 \xc3\x82l\xc3\xae</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Porte" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Porte">Sublime Porte</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The highest position in Islam, <i><a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">caliphate</a></i>, was claimed by the sultans starting with <a href="/wiki/Murad_I" title="Murad I">Murad I</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lambton_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambton-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> which was established as <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">Ottoman Caliphate</a>. The Ottoman sultan, <i><a href="/wiki/Padishah" title="Padishah">p\xc3\xa2di\xc5\x9f\xc3\xa2h</a></i> or "lord of kings", served as the Empire\'s sole regent and was considered to be the embodiment of its government, though he did not always exercise complete control. The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Harem" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Harem">Imperial Harem</a> was one of the most important powers of the Ottoman court. It was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Valide_Sultan" class="mw-redirect" title="Valide Sultan">Valide Sultan</a>. On occasion, the Valide Sultan would become involved in state politics. For a time, the women of the Harem effectively controlled the state in what was termed the "<a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_the_women" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of the women">Sultanate of Women</a>". New sultans were always chosen from the sons of the previous sultan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (September 2016)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Ottoman_Empire#Dubious" title="Talk:Ottoman Empire">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> The strong educational system of the <a href="/wiki/Palace_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace school">palace school</a> was geared towards eliminating the unfit potential heirs, and establishing support among the ruling elite for a successor. The palace schools, which would also educate the future administrators of the state, were not a single track. First, the <a href="/wiki/Madrasa" title="Madrasa">Madrasa</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>: <span lang="ota" dir="rtl">Medrese</span>&#8206;</i>) was designated for the Muslims, and educated scholars and state officials according to Islamic tradition. The financial burden of the Medrese was supported by vakifs, allowing children of poor families to move to higher social levels and income.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The second track was a free <a href="/wiki/Boarding_school" title="Boarding school">boarding school</a> for the Christians, the <i><a href="/wiki/Ender%C3%BBn" title="Ender\xc3\xbbn">Ender\xc3\xbbn</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> which recruited 3,000 students annually from Christian boys between eight and twenty years old from one in forty families among the communities settled in <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a> or the Balkans, a process known as <a href="/wiki/Devshirme_in_the_Ottoman_Palace_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Devshirme in the Ottoman Palace School">Devshirme</a> (<i><i lang="ota" title="Ottoman Turkish language text">Dev\xc5\x9firme</i></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Though the sultan was the supreme monarch, the sultan\'s political and executive authority was delegated. The politics of the state had a number of advisors and ministers gathered around a council known as <a href="/wiki/Divan" title="Divan">Divan</a>. The Divan, in the years when the Ottoman state was still a <i><a href="/wiki/Bey" title="Bey">Beylik</a></i>, was composed of the elders of the tribe. Its composition was later modified to include military officers and local elites (such as religious and political advisors). Later still, beginning in 1320, a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a> was appointed to assume certain of the sultan\'s responsibilities. The Grand Vizier had considerable independence from the sultan with almost unlimited powers of appointment, dismissal and supervision. Beginning with the late 16th century, sultans withdrew from politics and the Grand Vizier became the <i>de facto</i> head of state.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_p199_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_p199-143">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/220px-Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/330px-Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg/440px-Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="879" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yusuf_Ziya_Pa%C5%9Fa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yusuf_Ziya_Pasha" title="Yusuf Ziya Pasha">Yusuf Ziya Pasha</a>, Ottoman ambassador to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>, 1913</div></div></div>\n<p>Throughout Ottoman history, there were many instances in which local governors acted independently, and even in opposition to the ruler. After the Young Turk Revolution of 1908, the Ottoman state became a constitutional monarchy. The sultan no longer had executive powers. A parliament was formed, with representatives chosen from the provinces. The representatives formed the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Government_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Government of the Ottoman Empire">Imperial Government of the Ottoman Empire</a>.\n</p><p>This eclectic administration was apparent even in the diplomatic correspondence of the Empire, which was initially undertaken in the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek language</a> to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tughra" title="Tughra">Tughra</a> were calligraphic monograms, or signatures, of the Ottoman Sultans, of which there were 35. Carved on the Sultan\'s seal, they bore the names of the Sultan and his father. The statement and prayer, "ever victorious," was also present in most. The earliest belonged to <a href="/wiki/Orhan" title="Orhan">Orhan Gazi</a>. The ornately stylized <i>Tughra</i> spawned a branch of Ottoman-Turkish <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphy</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_law" title="Ottoman law">Ottoman law</a></div>\n<p>The Ottoman legal system accepted the <a href="/wiki/Religious_law" title="Religious law">religious law</a> over its subjects. At the same time the <i><a href="/wiki/Qanun_(law)" title="Qanun (law)">Qanun</a></i> (or <i>Kanun</i>), a secular legal system, co-existed with religious law or <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-otmkanun_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otmkanun-145">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman Empire was always organized around a system of local <a href="/wiki/Jurisprudence" title="Jurisprudence">jurisprudence</a>. Legal administration in the Ottoman Empire was part of a larger scheme of balancing central and local authority.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_109-110_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton_109-110-146">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Ottoman power revolved crucially around the administration of the rights to land, which gave a space for the local authority to develop the needs of the local <a href="/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Millet (Ottoman Empire)">millet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_109-110_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton_109-110-146">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The jurisdictional complexity of the Ottoman Empire was aimed to permit the integration of culturally and religiously different groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_109-110_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton_109-110-146">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman system had three court systems: one for Muslims, one for non-Muslims, involving appointed Jews and Christians ruling over their respective religious communities, and the "trade court". The entire system was regulated from above by means of the administrative <i>Qanun</i>, i.e. laws, a system based upon the Turkic <i><a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Yassa</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=T%C3%B6re_(law)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="T\xc3\xb6re (law) (page does not exist)">T\xc3\xb6re</a></i>, which were developed in the pre-Islamic era.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/220px-1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/330px-1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png/440px-1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="291" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1879-Ottoman_Court-from-NYL.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Ottoman trial, 1877</div></div></div>\n<p>These court categories were not, however, wholly exclusive: for instance, the Islamic courts, which were the Empire\'s primary courts, could also be used to settle a trade conflict or disputes between litigants of differing religions, and Jews and Christians often went to them to obtain a more forceful ruling on an issue. The Ottoman state tended not to interfere with non-Muslim religious law systems, despite legally having a voice to do so through local governors. The Islamic <i>Sharia</i> law system had been developed from a combination of the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur&#39;an">Qur\'an</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">Had\xc4\xabth</a>, or words of the prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_in_Islam" title="Muhammad in Islam">Muhammad</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Ijma" title="Ijma">ijm\xc4\x81\'</a></i>, or consensus of the members of the <a href="/wiki/Ummah" title="Ummah">Muslim community</a>; <a href="/wiki/Qiyas" title="Qiyas">qiyas</a>, a system of analogical reasoning from earlier precedents; and local customs. Both systems were taught at the Empire\'s law schools, which were in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bursa" title="Bursa">Bursa</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zibik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Zibik.jpg/220px-Zibik.jpg" width="220" height="336" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Zibik.jpg/330px-Zibik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Zibik.jpg/440px-Zibik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1850" data-file-height="2826" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zibik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An unhappy wife complains to the <a href="/wiki/Qadi" title="Qadi">Qadi</a> about her husband\'s impotence, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_miniature" title="Ottoman miniature">Ottoman miniature</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottoman Islamic legal system was set up differently from traditional European courts. Presiding over Islamic courts would be a <i>Qadi</i>, or judge. Since the closing of the <i><a href="/wiki/Ijtihad" title="Ijtihad">ijtihad</a></i>, or <i>Gate of Interpretation, Qadis </i>throughout the Ottoman Empire focused less on legal precedent, and more with local customs and traditions in the areas that they administered.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_109-110_146-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton_109-110-146">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> However, the Ottoman court system lacked an appellate structure, leading to jurisdictional case strategies where plaintiffs could take their disputes from one court system to another until they achieved a ruling that was in their favor.\n</p><p>In the late 19th century, the Ottoman legal system saw substantial reform. This process of legal modernization began with the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_G%C3%BClhane" title="Edict of G\xc3\xbclhane">Edict of G\xc3\xbclhane</a> of 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-review-niza_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-review-niza-147">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> These reforms included the "fair and public trial[s] of all accused regardless of religion," the creation of a system of "separate competences, religious and civil," and the validation of testimony on non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-int-handbook-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Specific land codes (1858), civil codes (1869\xe2\x80\x931876), and a code of civil procedure also were enacted.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-int-handbook-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These reforms were based heavily on French models, as indicated by the adoption of a three-tiered court system. Referred to as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nizamiye&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nizamiye (page does not exist)">Nizamiye</a>, this system was extended to the local magistrate level with the final promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Mecelle" title="Mecelle">Mecelle</a>, a civil code that regulated marriage, divorce, alimony, will, and other matters of personal status.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-int-handbook-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In an attempt to clarify the division of judicial competences, an administrative council laid down that religious matters were to be handled by religious courts, and statute matters were to be handled by the Nizamiye courts.<sup id="cite_ref-int-handbook_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-int-handbook-148">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Military of the Ottoman Empire">Military of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg/220px-Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg/330px-Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg/440px-Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="462" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walka_o_sztandar_turecki.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Sipahi" title="Sipahi">sipahis</a> in battle, holding the crescent banner (by <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Brandt" title="J\xc3\xb3zef Brandt">J\xc3\xb3zef Brandt</a>)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zapotocny.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zapotocny.jpg/220px-Zapotocny.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zapotocny.jpg/330px-Zapotocny.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zapotocny.jpg/440px-Zapotocny.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="761" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zapotocny.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman officers in Istanbul, 1897</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg/220px-Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg/330px-Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg/440px-Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="487" data-file-height="321" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nizami-cedid-ordusu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">Selim III</a> watching the parade of his new army, the <i><a href="/wiki/Nizam-i_Djedid" class="mw-redirect" title="Nizam-i Djedid">Nizam-\xc4\xb1 Cedid</a></i> (New Order) troops, in 1793</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg/220px-Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg/330px-Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg/440px-Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_pilots_in_1912.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Air Force">Ottoman pilots</a> in early 1912</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg/170px-Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg/255px-Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg/340px-Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="697" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ahmet_Ali_Celikten_in_flight_suit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ahmet_Ali_%C3%87elikten" title="Ahmet Ali \xc3\x87elikten">Ahmet Ali \xc3\x87elikten</a> is amongst the first black military pilots in history, clearly showing military diversification in the Ottoman Empire.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_1900.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Soldiers_1900.png/170px-Soldiers_1900.png" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Soldiers_1900.png/255px-Soldiers_1900.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Soldiers_1900.png/340px-Soldiers_1900.png 2x" data-file-width="570" data-file-height="748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_1900.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Military of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Imperial Army</a> in 1900</div></div></div>\n<p>The first military unit of the Ottoman State was an army that was organized by <a href="/wiki/Osman_I" title="Osman I">Osman I</a> from the tribesmen inhabiting the hills of western Anatolia in the late 13th century. The military system became an intricate organization with the advance of the Empire. The Ottoman military was a complex system of recruiting and fief-holding. The main corps of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Army">Ottoman Army</a> included <a href="/wiki/Janissary" class="mw-redirect" title="Janissary">Janissary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sipahi" title="Sipahi">Sipahi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akinci" class="mw-redirect" title="Akinci">Ak\xc4\xb1nc\xc4\xb1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_military_band" title="Ottoman military band">Mehter\xc3\xa2n</a>. The Ottoman army was once among the most advanced fighting forces in the world, being one of the first to use muskets and cannons. The Ottoman Turks began using <i><a href="/wiki/Falconet_(cannon)" title="Falconet (cannon)">falconets</a></i>, which were short but wide cannons, during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(1422)" title="Siege of Constantinople (1422)">Siege of Constantinople</a>. The Ottoman cavalry depended on high speed and mobility rather than heavy armour, using bows and short swords on fast <a href="/wiki/Turkoman_horse" title="Turkoman horse">Turkoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabian_horse" title="Arabian horse">Arabian</a> horses (progenitors of the <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred#Foundation_stallions" title="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a> racing horse),<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and often applied tactics similar to those of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, such as pretending to retreat while surrounding the enemy forces inside a crescent-shaped formation and then making the real attack. The Ottoman army continued to be an effective fighting force throughout the seventeenth and early eighteenth centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> falling behind the empire\'s European rivals only during a long period of peace from 1740\xe2\x80\x931768.<sup id="cite_ref-AksanOW_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AksanOW-22">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The modernization of the Ottoman Empire in the 19th century started with the military. In 1826 Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_II" title="Mahmud II">Mahmud II</a> abolished the Janissary corps and established the modern Ottoman army. He named them as the <a href="/wiki/Nizam-%C4%B1_Cedid" class="mw-redirect" title="Nizam-\xc4\xb1 Cedid">Nizam-\xc4\xb1 Cedid</a> (New Order). The Ottoman army was also the first institution to hire foreign experts and send its officers for training in western European countries. Consequently, the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">Young Turks</a> movement began when these relatively young and newly trained men returned with their education.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Ottoman Navy</a> vastly contributed to the expansion of the Empire\'s territories on the European continent. It initiated the conquest of North Africa, with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to the Ottoman Empire in 1517. Starting with the loss of <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> in 1821 and Algeria in 1830, Ottoman naval power and control over the Empire\'s distant overseas territories began to decline. Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClaziz" title="Abd\xc3\xbclaziz">Abd\xc3\xbclaziz</a> (reigned 1861\xe2\x80\x931876) attempted to reestablish a strong Ottoman navy, building the largest fleet after those of Britain and France. The shipyard at Barrow, England, built its first <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> in 1886 for the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-first_submarine_at_shipyard_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_submarine_at_shipyard-152">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg/220px-Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg/330px-Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="415" data-file-height="263" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Navy_at_the_Golden_Horn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A German postcard depicting the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Ottoman Navy</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a> in the early stages of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. At top left is a portrait of Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_V" title="Mehmed V">Mehmed V</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>However, the collapsing Ottoman economy could not sustain the fleet\'s strength for too long. Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClhamid_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd\xc3\xbclhamid II">Abd\xc3\xbclhamid II</a> distrusted the admirals who sided with the reformist <a href="/wiki/Midhat_Pasha" title="Midhat Pasha">Midhat Pasha</a>, and claimed that the large and expensive fleet was of no use against the Russians during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x9378)">Russo-Turkish War</a>. He locked most of the fleet inside the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horn" title="Golden Horn">Golden Horn</a>, where the ships decayed for the next 30 years. Following the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908, the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> sought to develop a strong Ottoman naval force. The <i>Ottoman Navy Foundation</i> was established in 1910 to buy new ships through public donations.\n</p><p>The establishment of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Air Force">Ottoman military aviation</a> dates back to between June 1909 and July 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The Ottoman Empire started preparing its first pilots and planes, and with the founding of the Aviation School (<i>Tayyare Mektebi</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Ye%C5%9Filk%C3%B6y" title="Ye\xc5\x9filk\xc3\xb6y">Ye\xc5\x9filk\xc3\xb6y</a> on 3 July 1912, the Empire began to tutor its own flight officers. The founding of the Aviation School quickened advancement in the military aviation program, increased the number of enlisted persons within it, and gave the new pilots an active role in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Army">Ottoman Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Navy</a>. In May 1913 the world\'s first specialized Reconnaissance Training Program was started by the Aviation School and the first separate reconnaissance division was established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In June 1914 a new military academy, the Naval Aviation School (<i>Bahriye Tayyare Mektebi</i>) was founded. With the outbreak of World War I, the modernization process stopped abruptly. The <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Squadrons_(Ottoman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviation Squadrons (Ottoman Empire)">Ottoman aviation squadrons</a> fought on many fronts during World War I, from <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a> in the west to the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> in the east and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> in the south.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Administrative divisions of the Ottoman Empire">Administrative divisions of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Empire_(1795).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png/220px-Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png/330px-Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png/440px-Ottoman_Empire_%281795%29.png 2x" data-file-width="2434" data-file-height="2037" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Empire_(1795).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eyalet" title="Eyalet">Eyalets</a> in 1795</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottoman Empire was first subdivided into provinces, in the sense of fixed territorial units with governors appointed by the sultan, in the late 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Imber_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imber-155">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eyalet" title="Eyalet">Eyalet</a> (also <i>Pashalik</i> or <i>Beylerbeylik</i>) was the territory of office of a <a href="/wiki/Beylerbey" title="Beylerbey">Beylerbey</a> (\xe2\x80\x9clord of lords\xe2\x80\x9d or governor), and was further subdivided in <a href="/wiki/Sanjaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanjaks">Sanjaks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Vilayets" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilayets">Vilayets</a> were introduced with the promulgation of the "Vilayet Law" (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Teskil-i Vilayet Nizamnamesi</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> in 1864, as part of the Tanzimat reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-trt_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trt-158">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Unlike the previous eyalet system, the 1864 law established a hierarchy of administrative units: the vilayet, <a href="/wiki/Liva_(sanjak)" class="mw-redirect" title="Liva (sanjak)">liva</a>/<a href="/wiki/Sanjak" title="Sanjak">sanjak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qadaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Qadaa">kaza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Town_council" title="Town council">village council</a>, to which the 1871 Vilayet Law added the <a href="/wiki/Nabiye" class="mw-redirect" title="Nabiye">nabiye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jpn_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpn-159">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Economic history of the Ottoman Empire">Economic history of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>\n<p>Ottoman government deliberately pursued a policy for the development of Bursa, Edirne, and Istanbul, successive Ottoman capitals, into major commercial and industrial centres, considering that merchants and artisans were indispensable in creating a new metropolis.<sup id="cite_ref-Inalcik1970209_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inalcik1970209-160">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> To this end, Mehmed and his successor Bayezid, also encouraged and welcomed migration of the Jews from different parts of Europe, who were settled in Istanbul and other port cities like Salonica. In many places in Europe, Jews were suffering persecution at the hands of their Christian counterparts, such as in Spain after the conclusion of Reconquista. The tolerance displayed by the Turks was welcomed by the immigrants.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehmed_the_Conqueror_(1432_%E2%80%931481).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg/220px-Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg/330px-Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg/440px-Mehmed_the_Conqueror_%281432_%E2%80%931481%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1197" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehmed_the_Conqueror_(1432_%E2%80%931481).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A European bronze medal from the period of <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Sultan Mehmed the Conqueror</a>, 1481</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ottoman economic mind was closely related to the basic concepts of state and society in the Middle East in which the ultimate goal of a state was consolidation and extension of the ruler\'s power, and the way to reach it was to get rich resources of revenues by making the productive classes prosperous.<sup id="cite_ref-Inalcik1970217_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inalcik1970217-161">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The ultimate aim was to increase the state revenues without damaging the prosperity of subjects to prevent the emergence of social disorder and to keep the traditional organization of the society intact. The Ottoman economy greatly expanded during the <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_Period" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern Period">Early Modern Period</a>, with particularly high growth rates during first half of the eighteenth century. The empire\'s annual income quadrupled between 1523 and 1748, adjusted for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The organization of the treasury and chancery were developed under the Ottoman Empire more than any other Islamic government and, until the 17th century, they were the leading organization among all their contemporaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_p199_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_p199-143">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> This organization developed a scribal bureaucracy (known as "men of the pen") as a distinct group, partly highly trained <a href="/wiki/Ulama" title="Ulama">ulama</a>, which developed into a professional body.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_p199_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_p199-143">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The effectiveness of this professional financial body stands behind the success of many great Ottoman statesmen.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Bank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ottoman_Bank.jpg/220px-Ottoman_Bank.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ottoman_Bank.jpg/330px-Ottoman_Bank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Ottoman_Bank.jpg/440px-Ottoman_Bank.jpg 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="363" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_Bank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Bank" title="Ottoman Bank">Ottoman Bank</a> was founded in 1856 in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>; in August 1896, the bank was <a href="/wiki/1896_Ottoman_Bank_takeover" class="mw-redirect" title="1896 Ottoman Bank takeover">captured</a> by members of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Armenian Revolutionary Federation</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Modern Ottoman studies indicate that the change in relations between the Ottoman Turks and central Europe was caused by the opening of the new sea routes. It is possible to see the decline in the significance of the land routes to the East as Western Europe opened the ocean routes that bypassed the Middle East and Mediterranean as parallel to the decline of the Ottoman Empire itself.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s).
